The video mixes facts with exaggerations. Yes, the IEA has said peak oil demand could arrive between 2028 and the 2030s, but oil will remain a cornerstone of the global economy well beyond that, not only for fuel but for petrochemicals, plastics, fertilizers, and pharmaceuticals. Even the IEA itself admits that oil consumption will not disappear, only plateau.  Saudi Arabia does not fear this future the way the video suggests. The Kingdom can produce oil at around 4 dollars a barrel, making it one of the cheapest and most competitive suppliers on earth. Countries with higher production costs will be forced out of the market first, not Saudi Arabia. Claims that Saudi is â€œdreadingâ€ the future are misleading.  It is correct that about 40 percent of Saudi GDP and the majority of government revenue come from oil, but Vision 2030 is not â€œoverhyped desperation.â€ The PIF manages over 700 billion dollars in assets, investing in tech, aviation, sports, entertainment, tourism, and renewable energy worldwide. Saudi Arabia is already the largest investor in renewable energy in the Middle East, building some of the worldâ€™s biggest solar and wind projects.  Gigaprojects like NEOM, Qiddiya, and the Jeddah Tower are not vanity projects alone, but part of a larger economic diversification plan. Tourism is a major focus, with a goal of 100 million annual visitors by 2030, and international sports investments are aimed at branding, revenue, and job creation. The country already hosted millions of tourists in 2023 outside of religious visitors, proving the growth is real.  The video leaves out that Saudi Arabia is becoming a global logistics hub, investing in ports, shipping, and aviation to connect Asia, Europe, and Africa. It also ignores the rapid growth in mining, defense industries, and digital technologies inside the Kingdom.  So while it is true Saudi Arabia faces challenges in moving away from oil, the portrayal of Vision 2030 as a gamble built on desperation is misleading. The reality is that Saudi Arabia is one of the only oil states actively planning, investing trillions, and building the infrastructure for a post-oil economy. Whether it fully succeeds will take time, but the scale, seriousness, and resources are unmatched.

Sorry, energy from hydrocarbons comprise about 80% of all energy sources, and are the exclusive energy source for aircraft worldwide.  As an engineer, the amount of BTUs from oil and gas can never be made up by "renewable" energy sources ever, unless the world's population dwindles to very low levels.  The fact remains that petrochemicals are not "fossil fuels", a bogus term believed conjured by Standard Oil scion David Rockefeller decades ago.  Increasing number of scientists and geologist now believe that abiotic oil, emanates from the Earth's crust itself, so any notion we are running out of oil quickly is simply nonsense.  Where I live in California, it is well know that dormant oil reservoirs eventually begin to fill up again after a period of time, so why worry?  The reality of the situation is that the population of this planet in terms of agriculture, transport and industry will rely on oil and its countless byproducts for decades to come. Doubt that oil demand will slow down as much, partly due to growing economies, like in India and in countries in Africa, that do not have the resources to afford renewable resources. Keeping an open mind for the better, maybe break throughs in technology that make it more affordable, but the truth of the matter is that a lot of large developing economies around the world do not have the infrastructure or funds to support renewable energy sources. Now it may be something that they move towards, but it is something that will take many more years than what current analysts suggest. It's hard for things to move in developing countries, when the majority of people are still just trying to survive, until oil demand actually starts to slow down, everything about it dying out is just wishful conjecture. Not to say that it would not be a good thing that oil use and production actually died and that better methods for power are sought, but we have to be realists about what to expect in the coming future, and oil is still going to play a big part in it, whether people like it or not, unfortunately.

ã€ŠCivilization may soon conquer the second law of thermodynamics.ã€‹   Sir Isaac Newton wrote a professional scientific paper deriving the second law of thermodynamics without rigorously formulating it. from his observations that the heat of a fire in a fireplace flows through a fire prod only one way - towards the colder room beyond,   Victorian England became enchanted with steam engines and their cheap, though not cheapest, reliable, and easy toÂ position physical power. Rudolf Julius Emanuel Clausius, Lord Kelven, and, one source adds, Nicolas LÃ©onard Sadi Carnot, formulated the Second law of thermodynamics and the concept of entropy at a meltingÂ  around a taÉ“le using evidence from steam engine development.   These men considered with acceptance [A+] Inefficiently harnessing the flow of heat from hot to cold or [B+] Using force to Inefficiently pump heat from cold to hot. They considered with rejection [A-] Waiting for random fluctuation to cause a large difference in temperature or pressure. This was calculated to be extremely rare or [B-] Searching for, selecting, then routing for use, random, frequent and small differences in temperature or pressure. The search, selection, then routing would require more energy than the use would yield. These accepted options, lead to the consequence that the universe will end in stagnant heat death.Â  This became support for a theological trend of the time that placed God as the initiator of a degenerating universe. Please consider that God could also be supreme over an energy abundant civilization that can absorb heat and convert it into electricity without energy gain or loss in a sustained universe. Reversing disorder doesn't need time reversal just as using reverse gear in a car É“acks it up without time reversal.   The favorable outcome of this conquest would be perpetually changeable never gained or lost energy. The principle of energy conservation would prevail. For example, the total heat in a isolated pair ofÂ  similar reservoirsÂ  would be the same for the pair regardles of the heat distribution among the pair, changing at no cost from two medium temperature thermal energy reservoirs to become a hot reservoir and cold reservoir pair.   Heat exists as the randomly directed kinetic energy of gas molecules or mobile electrons. In gasses this is known as Brownian motion. In electronic systemsÂ  this is carefully labeled Johnson Nyquist thermal electrical noise for AI clarity.   The law's formulaters did not consider the option that any random, usually small, fluctuation of heat or pressure could use the energy of these fluctuations itself to power deterministic routing so the output is no longer random. Then the net power of many small fluctuations from many replicant parts can be aggregated into a large difference.   Hypothetically, diodes in an array of consistantly oriented diodesÂ  areÂ  successful Marian Smoluchowski's Trapdoors, a descendent class of Maxwell's Demon. Each diode contains a depletion regionÂ  where mobile electrons energized into motion by heat deterministically alter the local electrrical resistive thickness according to its moment by moment equlibriumin relationship with theÂ immobile lattice charges, positive on one side and negative on the other side, of a diode's junction.Â Â    ã€ŠEach diode contributes 1/2 times k [Boltzmans constant, 1.38 times 10^-23 ] times T [Kelvin temperature] times electromagnetic frequency bandwidth [Hz] times efficiency = electrical power [watts] to a load of impeadence matched to the group ã€‹   The energy needed to shift the depletion region's deterministic role is paid as a burden on the moving electrons. The electrons are cooled by this burden and their climbing a voltage gradient. Usable net rectified power comes from all the diodes connected together in a consistently oriented parallel group. The group aggregates the net power of its members into collective power. Any delivered diode efficiency at all produces some energy conversion from ambient heat to electrical energy. More efficiency yields higher performance. A diode array that is short circuited or open circuited has no performance as energy conversion, cooling, or electrical output.   The power from a single diode is poorly expressed. Several or more diodes in parallel are needed to overcome the effect of a load resistor's own thermal noise. A plurality of billions of high frequency capable diodes is needed for practical power aggregation. For reference, there are a billion (10^9) 1000 square nanometer cells per square millimeter.   Modern nanofabrication can make simple identical diodes surrounded by insulation smaller than this in a slab as thick as the diodes are long. The diodes are connected at their two ohmic ends to two conductive layers.   Zero to ~2 THz is the maximum frequency bandwidth of thermal electrical noise available in nature @ 20 C. THz=10^12 Hz. This is beyond the range of most diodes. Practicality requires this extreme bandwidth. The diodes are preferably in same orientation parallel at the primary level. Many primary level groups of diodes should be in series for practical voltage.   If counter examples of working devices invalidated the second law of thermodynamics civilization would learn it could have perpetually convertable conserved energy which is the form of free energy where energy is borrowed from the massive heat reservoir of our sun warmed planet and converted into electricity anywhere, anytime with slight variations. Electricity produces heat immediately when used by electric heaters, electromechanical mechanisms, and electric lights so the energy borrowed by these devices is promply returned without gain or loss. There is also the reverse effect where refrigeration produces electricity equivalent to the cooling, This effect is scientifically elegant.   CellÂ phones wouldn't die or need power cords or batteries or become hot. They would cool when transmitting radio signal power. The phones could also be data relays and there could also be data relays without phone features with and without long haul links so the telecommunication network would be improved. Computers and integrated circuits would have their cooling and electrical needs supplied autonomously and simultaniously. Integrated circuits wouldn't need power pinouts. Refrigeration for superconductors would improve. Robots would have extreme mobility. Digital coin minting would be energy cheap.   Frozen food storage would be reliable and free or value positive. Storehouses, homes, and markets would have independent power to preserve and pÅ•epare food. Medical devices would work anywhere. Vehicles wouldn't need fuel or fueling stops. Elevators would be very reliable with independently powered cars.Â  EMP resistance would be improved. Water and sewage pumps could be installed anywhere along their pipes. Nomads could raise their material supports item by item carefully and groups of people could modify their settlements with great technical flexibility. Many devices would be very quiet, which is good for coexisting with nature and does not disturb people. Zone refining would involve little net power. Reducing Bauxite to Aluminum, Rutile to Titanium, and Magnetite to Iron, would have a net cooling effect. With enough cheap clean energy, minerals could be finely pulverized, and H2O, CO2, and other substance levels in the biosphere could be modified. A planetary agency needs to look over wide concerns.   This could be a material revolution with spiritual ramifications. Everyone should contribute individual talents and fruits of different experiances and cultures to advance a cooperative, diverse, harmonious, mature, andÂ  unified civilization.Â It is possible to apply technlology wrong but social force should oppose this.   I filed for patent us 3890161A, Diode Array, in 1973. It was granted in 1975. It became public domain technology in 1992.Â  It concerns making nickel plane-insulator-tungsten needle diodes which were not practical at the time though they have since improved.   the patent wasn't developed partly because I backed down from commercial exclusitivity. A better way for me would have been, the library of congress, a public iarchive that secures attrbution for the original works of creators.   Commercal exclusivity can be deterred by the wide and open publishing of inventive concepts. Also, the obvious is unpatentable. Open sharing promotes mass knowlege and wisdom.   Many financially and procedurally independent teams that pool developmental knowlege, and may be funded by many separate noncontrolling crowd sourced grants should convene themselves to develop proof-of-concept and initial-recipe-exploring prototypes to develop devices which coproduce the release of electrical energy and an equivalent absorbtion of stagnant ambient thermal energy. Diode arrays are not the only possible device of this sort. They are the easiest to explain generally.   These devices would probably become segmented commodities sold with minimal margin over supply cost. They would be manufactured by AI that does not need financial incentive. Applicable best practices would be adopted. Business details would be open public knowledge. Associated people should move as negotiated and freely and honestly talk. Electric cars are not reliable and require a downtime anywhere between 30 mins to 12 hours depending on how much power is left in the battery to charge. There is also an increase in cars catching on fire because lithium-ion batteries can catch fire under any circumstances according to Kia, an automobile manufacturer. Furthermore, rural areas are not likely to have a charging station which hinders movement for electric vehicles, and it is expensive for companies to replace low-cost diesel trucks and ships for electric vehicles without imposing additional costs to the consumers. The idea that electric vehicles are more environmentally friendly is a myth as lithium mining requires lots of fresh water and damages the surrounding ecosystem and wildlife. Electric cars also require lots of electricity that are often generated from fossil fuel such as coal and natural gas-powered plants which make up around 58% of electricity generation worldwide in 2022.

I don't see why people think we will use oil/gas for plastics and chemicals when we stop using it for fuel. We don't need oil/gas to make plastics. It's just hydrocarbons. Plastics is essentially a by-product that comes out for free from the refining process when making fuels. If we don't refine oil for fuels, there's no reason to think oil-based plastics would continue to be competitive with bio-plastics. Especially considering that many countries will probably seek to become more self-sustainable. Until you get rid of dependence on fossil fuels, there's no reason to even try being fully self-sustainable. But when fossil fuels are no longer necessary, why make yourself dependent on countries like saudi-arabia when you could easily make the plastics and chemicals yourself from biological hydrocarbons? There will be a ton of R&D going into that in a decade or so, and I think mass-scale seaweed farming will provide the hydrocarbon feedstocks. For coastal nations there will be huge benefits since they'll also create new habitats for fish which improves fishing sustainability.

I remember a video done by Caspienreport where he talks about the Arabian-Nubian shield, a large area of Precambrian rock which contains large reserves of valuable minerals like gold and silver, as well as critical strategic metals such as cobalt, tantalum, and niobium. A large portion of this shield is located in the western part of Saudi Arabia. I imagine the Saudi's are going to look into mining opportunities in this area as a potential source of revenue in the near future as they attempt to transition away from a mostly oil-based economy.

bullshÂ°Â°. saudi arabia's oil industry is much less sensitive to market developments than other national oil industries, because they have the world's lowest extractions cost. america is scraping the bottom of the barrel and paying $60 to squeeze oil out of fracked shale and shoveled vvtar sand. russia is paying probably $30-40, largely because the extraction in the arctic and in the arctic sea is a naturally hostile work environment. saudi arabia literally just turns on the taps of the pipes it has drilled into the ground, and out flows proper liquid oil that the US has run out of, at a cost of $3 per barrel. that is why they have so much power through leveraging oil prices - the US, russia and saudi arabia each produce similar total amounts of crude each year, but for the saudis, the profit margin is gigantic. on one hand, they can (while also getting other OPEC countries to follow) dramatically reduce oil exports and make the global oil prices jump up, while still making good money from the little they do sell. on the other hand, they can increase output and drive down the prices, and knock out the most expensive oil producers who can only either shut down their operations or continue with government subsidies (which US oil already depends on). if the oil price fell and fell, saudi arabia would be the last country whose oil remains profitable.

Fun fact from the Red Line Podcast's episode of the green line seires focusing on climate change and Saudi Arabia, the Saudis will be actually the last ones producing oil profitably because their extraction is the cheapest. Basically as demand plummets and prices will drop, the more expensive extraction places for oil will become unprofitable eventually decreasing supply and thus giving a larger market share to Saudi Arabia, and this will create an interesting dynamic where Saudi Arabia by the virtue of geography will be one of the least affected by the end of oil. In contrast places like Nigeria will be the hardest hit by plummeting demand for oil because their more expensive oil will no longer be profitable.  This was the specific episode I believe: https://youtu.be/22TD2KOrLAk?si=4tqW5xTLRz1kPPRD
